# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Task: Kubelet Container Manager Architecture Guide

**Repository:** kubernetes/kubernetes (stripped snapshot)
**Output:** Write your document to `/workspace/documentation.md`

## Objective

Produce a subsystem architecture guide for kubelet container manager, including resource manager interactions and platform variance.

## Scope

Focus on the kubelet container manager subsystem.
Your document must explain component responsibilities, end-to-end flow, and extension or operational tradeoffs.

## Content Expectations

Address all of the following in your own structure:
- subsystem purpose, boundaries, and upstream/downstream dependencies
- key components and how responsibilities are split
- end-to-end control/request flow with concrete repository evidence
- failure modes, limits, and design tradeoffs
- extension points, customization hooks, and associated risks
- a concise map of the most important files/directories used in your analysis

## Quality Bar

- Cite concrete file paths from the repository.
- Explain behavior and interactions, not just API signatures.
- Include at least one section on operational implications (performance, reliability, or maintainability).
- Do not fabricate classes, functions, or files.

## Anti-Requirements

- Do not output `doc.go`.
- Do not provide shallow bullet dumps without system flow explanation.
- Do not rely on external docs not present in the workspace.


## Artifact-Only Evaluation

You are in **artifact-only mode**. Your workspace is empty — all code discovery
must go through Sourcegraph MCP tools. Express all code changes as **unified
diffs** in your output artifact (e.g., `fix_patch` fields in review.json, or a
standalone `solution.patch` file). Do NOT attempt to edit source files directly
— there are no source files in your workspace.

Input
{
  "content": "# Kubelet Container Manager Architecture Guide\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries\n\nThe kubelet container manager subsystem is responsible for managing the complete lifecycle of containers and pods on a Kubernetes node. It serves as the critical interface between the Kubernetes control plane's desired pod specifications and the actual container runtime (Docker, containerd, CRI-O, etc.) through the Container Runtime Interface (CRI).\n\n### Purpose\n\n- **Container Lifecycle Management**: Create, start, stop, and delete containers with proper ordering and resource allocation\n- **Resource Enforcement**: Apply CPU limits, memory reservations, and device allocations through cgroups\n- **Pod Orchestration**: Coordinate sandbox creation and container dependencies (init containers, ephemeral containers, app containers)\n- **State Reconciliation**: Drive containers toward desired state through repeated synchronization cycles\n- **Garbage Collection**: Remove unused containers and images to prevent resource exhaustion\n\n### Boundaries\n\n**Upstream Dependencies**:\n- **Pod Specifications** (`v1.Pod`): Desired pod configuration from API server\n- **Pod Status**: Current runtime state queried from container runtime\n- **Configuration Sources**: File-based manifests, API server, HTTP endpoints\n- **Resource Allocations**: From device plugins, CPU/memory managers, and topology managers\n\n**Downstream Dependencies**:\n- **Container Runtime Interface (CRI)**: gRPC service for pod/container operations\n- **Cgroup Managers** (Linux): Apply resource limits via cgroup filesystems\n- **Volume Mounts**: Storage subsystem for ephemeral and persistent volumes\n- **Network Plugins**: CNI for pod networking (handled separately in kubelet)\n\n**External Services**:\n- Image registry access for container image pulls\n- Kubelet's own node status and eviction managers\n- Pod lifecycle hooks (pre-start, post-stop handlers)\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 2.1 Runtime Interface Layer\n\n**File**: `pkg/kubelet/container/runtime.go`\n\nThe `Runtime` interface defines the contract that all container runtimes must implement:\n\n```\nRuntime interface provides:\n- SyncPod(ctx, pod, podStatus, pullSecrets, backOff, restartAllContainers) \u2192 PodSyncResult\n  Orchestrates pod creation/updates, the primary entry point\n\n- KillPod(ctx, pod, runningPod, gracePeriodOverride) \u2192 error\n  Terminates all containers in a pod with grace period\n\n- GetPodStatus(ctx, uid, name, namespace) \u2192 *PodStatus\n  Queries runtime for current pod state\n\n- GarbageCollect(ctx, gcPolicy, allSourcesReady, evictNonDeletedPods) \u2192 error\n  Cleans up dead containers per policy\n\n- ImageService: PullImage, ListImages, RemoveImage operations\n```\n\nThis interface allows multiple runtime implementations to be plugged in, though the dominant implementation is `kubeGenericRuntimeManager`.\n\n### 2.2 Concrete Runtime Manager\n\n**File**: `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_manager.go`\n\n`kubeGenericRuntimeManager` is the main orchestration component. It holds:\n\n**Critical Dependencies**:\n- `runtimeService` (internalapi.RuntimeService): gRPC client to actual container runtime\n- `imageService` (internalapi.ImageManagerService): gRPC client for image operations\n- `containerManager` (cm.ContainerManager): Resource allocation and cgroup enforcement\n- `livenessManager`, `readinessManager`, `startupManager`: Probe result caching\n- `containerGC`: Garbage collector for dead containers\n- `internalLifecycle` (cm.InternalContainerLifecycle): Resource manager hooks\n\n**Key Responsibilities**:\n1. Translate Kubernetes pod specs to CRI sandbox/container configurations\n2. Orchestrate container creation sequence (init \u2192 app \u2192 ephemeral)\n3. Manage image pulling with credential providers and retry logic\n4. Coordinate with resource managers for CPU, memory, device allocation\n5. Track container state transitions and generate events\n\n### 2.3 Resource Management Layer\n\n**File**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go`\n\nThe `ContainerManager` interface defines the resource enforcement subsystem:\n\n```\nContainerManager interface manages:\n- System cgroups (kubelet, runtime, system processes)\n- Pod-level cgroups and QoS hierarchies\n- CPU allocation policies (none, static)\n- Memory management and reservation\n- Device plugin resources\n- Topology-aware resource placement\n- Pod admission and pre-flight checks\n- Node allocatable enforcement\n```\n\n**Linux Implementation**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go`\n\nCreates and manages three cgroup hierarchies:\n\n1. **System Cgroups**: Container for kubelet/runtime processes\n2. **Kubelet Cgroups**: Limits on kubelet itself\n3. **Pod Cgroups**: Hierarchy where each pod gets a cgroup based on QoS class\n   - `kubepods` (burstable) \u2192 pod cgroup \u2192 container cgroups\n   - `kubepods-burstable` (burstable) \u2192 pod cgroup \u2192 container cgroups\n   - `kubepods-besteffort` (besteffort) \u2192 pod cgroup \u2192 container cgroups\n\n### 2.4 Pod Container Manager\n\n**File**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/pod_container_manager_linux.go`\n\nManages pod-level cgroup creation and resource configuration:\n\n**Responsibilities**:\n- Create pod-level cgroup if QoS cgroup hierarchy is enabled\n- Apply pod-level CPU and memory limits before container creation\n- Handle MemoryQoS settings (cgroup v2 memory throttling)\n- Enforce PID limits at pod scope\n- Update pod resource configuration dynamically\n\n### 2.5 Resource Managers (Pluggable)\n\nThe container manager coordinates with specialized resource managers through `InternalContainerLifecycle` hooks:\n\n**pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager**: CPU affinity and exclusive CPU allocation\n- Policies: `none` (no affinity), `static` (pinning for Guaranteed pods)\n- Topology-aware placement via NodeInfo topology\n\n**pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager**: Memory affinity for NUMA systems\n- Memory allocation based on topology hints\n- Manages memory reservation per pod\n\n**pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager**: Device plugin resource allocation\n- Tracks device availability from plugins\n- Allocates devices to containers via mounts and environment\n\n**pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager**: Coordinate CPU, memory, and device allocation\n- Collects topology hints from all managers\n- Ensures aligned allocation or fails pod admission\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control and Request Flow\n\n### 3.1 Pod Synchronization Flow (Main Orchestration)\n\n**Entry Point**: `kubeGenericRuntimeManager.SyncPod()` in `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_manager.go:1394`\n\n```\nSyncPod orchestrates 8 sequential steps:\n\nStep 1: Compute Sandbox and Container Changes\n\u251c\u2500 Call computePodActions(pod, podStatus, restartAllContainers)\n\u251c\u2500 Determine what needs killing, creating, or resizing\n\u2514\u2500 Identify sandbox changes (network, security context)\n\nStep 2: Kill Pod Sandbox if Necessary\n\u251c\u2500 If sandbox changed: stop all containers and remove sandbox\n\u2514\u2500 Purge init containers for clean restart\n\nStep 3: Kill Unwanted Containers\n\u251c\u2500 For each container marked for termination\n\u251c\u2500 Call killContainer(pod, containerID, gracePeriod)\n\u2514\u2500 Handle in-place restart container removals\n\nStep 4: Create Pod Sandbox\n\u251c\u2500 generatePodSandboxConfig(pod) \u2192 CRI config\n\u2502  \u251c\u2500 Metadata (name, UID, attempt count)\n\u2502  \u251c\u2500 DNS configuration\n\u2502  \u251c\u2500 Network namespace mode (host/container/none)\n\u2502  \u251c\u2500 Security context (SELinux, AppArmor, seccomp)\n\u2502  \u2514\u2500 RuntimeClass handler lookup\n\u251c\u2500 Call runtimeService.RunPodSandbox(config, handler)\n\u2514\u2500 Store returned sandboxID for containers\n\nStep 5: Create Ephemeral Containers\n\u251c\u2500 For each ephemeral container spec\n\u2514\u2500 createContainer() with copy-on-write semantics\n\nStep 6: Create Init Containers\n\u251c\u2500 Containers execute in order (must complete)\n\u251c\u2500 Each init container waits for previous one\n\u2514\u2500 Handles init container restarts\n\nStep 7: Resize Running Containers (if InPlacePodVerticalScaling)\n\u251c\u2500 For Guaranteed QoS pods\n\u251c\u2500 Call runtimeService.RespawnContainer()\n\u2514\u2500 Adjust CPU/memory allocations\n\nStep 8: Create Normal Application Containers\n\u251c\u2500 Containers run in parallel (optional)\n\u251c\u2500 generateContainerConfig() for each container\n\u251c\u2500 Call createContainer() for each\n\u2514\u2500 Start all containers\n```\n\n### 3.2 Container Creation Sequence\n\n**File**: `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_container.go`\n\nFor each container, the flow is:\n\n```\ncreateContainer(ctx, pod, container):\n  1. generateContainerConfig(pod, container)\n     \u251c\u2500 Image with runtime handler (e.g., nvidia for GPU)\n     \u251c\u2500 Command, args, env variables\n     \u251c\u2500 Mounts (volumes, tmpfs, secrets)\n     \u251c\u2500 Devices (block, character, CDI devices)\n     \u251c\u2500 Port mappings\n     \u2514\u2500 Security context (capabilities, SELinux, user namespace)\n\n  2. Lifecycle hook: PreCreateContainer()\n     \u251c\u2500 Call containerManager.InternalContainerLifecycle\n     \u2514\u2500 (CPU/memory manager setup, topology hints)\n\n  3. Ensure pod container exists (pod cgroup)\n     \u2514\u2500 containerManager.NewPodContainerManager().EnsureExists()\n\n  4. Call runtimeService.CreateContainer(sandboxID, containerConfig)\n     \u2514\u2500 Runtime creates container (not started yet)\n\n  5. Lifecycle hook: PreStartContainer()\n     \u251c\u2500 CPU manager: AddContainer(pod, container, containerID)\n     \u251c\u2500 Memory manager: AddContainer(pod, container, containerID)\n     \u2514\u2500 Topology manager: AddContainer(pod, container, containerID)\n\n  6. Call runtimeService.StartContainer(containerID)\n     \u2514\u2500 Container starts executing\n```\n\n### 3.3 Pod Status Query Flow\n\n**File**: `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_manager.go`\n\nCalled by kubelet's status manager to fetch current pod state:\n\n```\nGetPodStatus(ctx, uid, name, namespace):\n  1. Call runtimeService.PodSandboxStatus(sandboxID)\n  2. For each container in pod:\n     \u2514\u2500 Call runtimeService.ContainerStatus(containerID)\n  3. Extract status fields:\n     \u251c\u2500 State (created, running, exited)\n     \u251c\u2500 Creation/start/finish times\n     \u251c\u2500 Exit code and reason\n     \u251c\u2500 Restart count\n     \u251c\u2500 Resource usage (if available)\n     \u2514\u2500 Mount information\n  4. Aggregate into PodStatus{\n       IPs, ContainerStatuses[], SandboxStatuses[]\n     }\n```\n\n### 3.4 Garbage Collection Flow\n\n**File**: `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_gc.go`\n\nRuns periodically to clean up dead containers:\n\n```\nGarbageCollect(ctx, gcPolicy, allSourcesReady, evictNonDeletedPods):\n  1. List all containers from runtime\n  2. Group containers by (pod UID, container name)\n  3. For each group, keep only N most recent containers per policy:\n     \u251c\u2500 maxPerPodContainer (default 5)\n     \u251c\u2500 maxContainers (default 100)\n     \u2514\u2500 minAge (default 1 minute)\n  4. Mark excess containers for removal\n  5. If allSourcesReady:\n     \u251c\u2500 Also GC containers from unknown pods\n     \u2514\u2500 (pods not in current pod list)\n  6. Stop containers before removal (with grace period)\n  7. Call runtimeService.RemoveContainer(containerID)\n  8. Similarly GC sandboxes (but less aggressive)\n```\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Container Lifecycle Failures\n\n**Sandbox Creation Failures**\n- **Cause**: Network namespace creation fails, SELinux context invalid, resource quota exceeded\n- **Behavior**: Pod marked as failed, containers never created\n- **Recovery**: Retry mechanism with exponential backoff, user must inspect logs and fix spec\n\n**Container Creation Timeouts**\n- **Cause**: Image pull hangs (network), runtime unresponsive\n- **Behavior**: Timeout after default 5 minutes, pod in pending state\n- **Recovery**: Event recorded, retry on next sync cycle\n\n**Resource Allocation Failures**\n- **Cause**: Insufficient CPUs for static affinity, devices unavailable, memory quota exceeded\n- **Behavior**: Pod admission rejected before containers created\n- **Recovery**: Requires resource freeing (other pod eviction) or reducing request\n\n**Container Startup Failures**\n- **Cause**: Application crashed immediately, bad command, permission denied\n- **Behavior**: Container exits quickly, restart policy determines action\n- **Recovery**: Restart loop with exponential backoff (RestartPolicy)\n\n### 4.2 Operational Limits\n\n**Container Count Per Pod**\n- No hard limit in kubelet\n- Practical limit: ~100 containers per pod (scheduling, network overhead)\n- Cgroup management overhead increases linearly\n\n**Container Image Sizes**\n- Runtime-dependent, typically limited by node disk\n- Large images cause longer pull times, delays pod startup\n- Multiple images on same layer share storage (deduplication depends on runtime)\n\n**Grace Period for Shutdown**\n- Default: 30 seconds per pod\n- Minimum: 2 seconds (hardcoded in kuberuntime)\n- Enforced by kubelet + runtime; hard kill (SIGKILL) after grace expires\n\n**Cgroup Resource Limits**\n- CPU shares: integer 2-262144, no unit enforced by cgroup\n- Memory: bytes only, no swap separate from memory (cgroup v1 vs v2 difference)\n- CPU quota: enforces hard limit if cpuCFSQuota enabled\n\n### 4.3 Key Design Tradeoffs\n\n**Sandbox-per-Pod Architecture**\n- **Tradeoff**: One network namespace per pod vs. per-container networking\n- **Rationale**: Simplifies pod networking (all containers share pod IP), matches Kubernetes model\n- **Cost**: Cannot change pod network isolation after creation; sandbox recreation needed\n\n**Preemptive Kill vs. Graceful Termination**\n- **Tradeoff**: Always allow grace period vs. fast cleanup\n- **Rationale**: Respect application shutdown hooks (SIGTERM \u2192 graceful, SIGKILL after)\n- **Cost**: Delayed eviction; can be overridden for node pressure scenarios\n\n**Pod Cgroup Hierarchy**\n- **Tradeoff**: Pod-level cgroup limits vs. per-container granularity\n- **Rationale**: Enforce minimum QoS guarantees at pod scope; QoS class coordination\n- **Cost**: Cannot exceed pod limit even if individual containers idle; less fine-grained control\n\n**Stateless Container Manager**\n- **Tradeoff**: Recompute state every sync cycle vs. in-memory tracking\n- **Rationale**: Resilient to kubelet restarts, always consistent with runtime ground truth\n- **Cost**: Repeated runtime queries; overhead for large pod counts\n\n**ImagePullBackOff vs. Error Distinction**\n- **Tradeoff**: Retry image pulls indefinitely vs. fail fast on bad image\n- **Rationale**: Network transients are common; bad images should retry (user may push fix)\n- **Cost**: User confusion on actually bad images (typos in name, auth failures)\n\n## 5. Extension Points, Customization Hooks, and Associated Risks\n\n### 5.1 Internal Container Lifecycle Hooks\n\n**File**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/internal_container_lifecycle.go`\n\nThree extension points during container creation:\n\n```go\ntype InternalContainerLifecycle interface {\n    // Called after container config generated, before CRI CreateContainer\n    PreCreateContainer(pod, container, containerConfig)\n\n    // Called after runtimeService.StartContainer\n    PreStartContainer(pod, container, containerID)\n\n    // Called after container stopped, before removal\n    PostStopContainer(containerID)\n}\n```\n\n**Current Implementations**:\n- **CPU Manager** (`PreStartContainer`): Pins CPUs for Guaranteed pods\n- **Memory Manager** (`PreStartContainer`): Applies memory affinity\n- **Topology Manager** (`PreStartContainer` and `PostStopContainer`): Coordinates all managers\n\n**Risk**: Bugs in custom hooks block container startup; pod creation hangs if hook panics\n\n### 5.2 RuntimeClass Handler Selection\n\n**File**: `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_sandbox.go:58`\n\nAllows selecting alternative runtime handlers per pod:\n\n```go\nruntimeHandler, err := m.runtimeClassManager.LookupRuntimeHandler(pod.Spec.RuntimeClassName)\n// Passed to runtimeService.RunPodSandbox(..., runtimeHandler)\n```\n\n**Use Cases**:\n- GPU workloads (nvidia, amd handlers)\n- Kata Containers for isolation\n- Custom runtime configurations\n\n**Risk**: Handler misconfiguration silently falls back to default; wrong isolation if handler unavailable\n\n### 5.3 Device Plugin Integration\n\n**File**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/device_manager`\n\nDevice managers expose custom resources:\n\n```go\ncontainerManager.UpdatePluginResources(nodeInfo, podAdmitAttributes)\n// Returns allocated devices via:\ncontainerManager.GetResources(ctx, pod, container)\n```\n\n**Extension Pattern**:\n1. Plugin registers via kubelet plugin watcher\n2. Device manager discovers available resources\n3. On pod admission: topology manager allocates devices\n4. On container creation: GetResources returns mounts, env vars, annotations\n\n**Risk**: Plugin not responding causes pod admission hangs; resource leaks if plugin crashes\n\n### 5.4 Pre-Admit Handlers\n\n**File**: Referenced by `containerManager.GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler()`\n\nPods are admitted before scheduling (kubelet-local gate):\n\n```\nPodAdmitHandler is called:\n  Before any containers created\n  With pod and all current active pods\n  Can reject pod or modify resource allocations\n```\n\n**Use Cases**:\n- Custom admission control (security policies)\n- Dynamic capacity tracking beyond kubelet-reported\n- Pod resource overcommit enforcement\n\n**Risk**: Rejecting pods here bypasses API server validation; inconsistent with scheduler decisions\n\n### 5.5 Image Credential Providers\n\n**File**: `pkg/kubelet/images/pullmanager`\n\nCustom executables can provide registry credentials:\n\n```\nCredential Provider Plugin:\n  Input: image reference\n  Output: username/password or bearer token\n  Executed as subprocess during image pull\n  Can be slow (synchronous in critical path)\n```\n\n**Risk**: Slow credential providers delay all pod startup; credential exposure in logs if not careful\n\n## 6. Operational Implications\n\n### 6.1 Performance Characteristics\n\n**Container Startup Latency**\n- Sandbox creation: 10-50ms (depends on network namespace setup, cgroup creation)\n- Image pull: seconds to minutes (network bound, registry latency)\n- Container creation: 50-200ms per container (runtime-dependent)\n- Container start: 0-5000ms (application dependent, health probe startup)\n- **Total first pod**: seconds to minutes (dominated by image pull)\n- **Total subsequent pod** (cached image): hundreds of milliseconds\n\n**Resource Manager Overhead**\n- CPU manager affinity computation: O(n) where n = CPU count\n- Topology manager hint collection: 3-5ms per container (gathers from CPU/memory/device managers)\n- Cgroup creation: ~1-10ms per pod (filesystem operations)\n- **Scaling limit**: ~100 containers on single node before noticeable delay\n\n**Garbage Collection Overhead**\n- Lists all containers from runtime: O(n) where n = total containers ever created\n- Typical: <100ms for nodes with ~100 total containers\n- **Risk**: GC pause blocks pod operations if many dead containers\n\n### 6.2 Reliability and Resilience\n\n**Recovery from Kubelet Restart**\n- On restart, kubelet queries runtime for all pods and containers\n- Containers continue running under runtime; kubelet re-syncs state\n- **Safe**: Long-running pods unaffected; state consistent from runtime ground truth\n- **Risk**: If container runtime crashed, kubelet cannot detect state; assumes runtime recovery\n\n**Handling Hung Container Runtime**\n- All CRI calls timeout after default 2 minutes\n- Timeout causes pod to be marked failed; events recorded\n- **Limitation**: Cannot forcefully kill runtime; depends on external monitoring\n\n**Orphaned Containers**\n- If kubelet crashes, containers keep running\n- Upon restart: kubelet reattaches via container ID matching\n- **Risk**: If containers deleted from runtime externally, kubelet has stale state (pod never terminates)\n\n### 6.3 Resource Accounting and Limits\n\n**Memory Pressure Handling**\n- Node eviction manager uses cgroup memory.max + usage to trigger eviction\n- Container manager enforces memory.max at pod scope\n- **Limitation**: No memory overcommit enforcement; OOMKiller is last resort\n- **Tuning**: `--memory-manager-policy=static` for guaranteed allocations\n\n**CPU Throttling**\n- CPU limits enforced via cpu.cfs_quota_us / cpu.cfs_period_us\n- CPU manager reserves CPUs for Guaranteed pods (no sharing)\n- **Limitation**: Noisy neighbor problem if bursting pods on same node\n- **Tuning**: `--cpu-manager-policy=static` + CPU topology hints\n\n**Disk I/O Limits**\n- Not enforced by container manager (delegated to runtime/systemd)\n- Cleanup policy for images/logs relies on simple age/count heuristics\n- **Risk**: Slow disk I/O can stall pod startup\n\n### 6.4 Observability and Debugging\n\n**Event Recording**\n- Pod events recorded on key transitions (SandboxChanged, ContainerBackOff, etc.)\n- Events help operators understand failure reasons\n- **Limitation**: No structured logs of internal decisions; must read kubelet logs\n\n**Metrics Exported**\n- `kubelet_pod_worker_duration_seconds`: Time to sync pod\n- `kubelet_container_manager_*`: Resource manager metrics (CPU affinity, etc.)\n- `kubelet_runtime_crio_operations_duration_seconds`: CRI call latencies (per operation type)\n- **Gap**: No metrics on sandbox/container state mismatches\n\n**Pod Log Access**\n- Kubelet reads container logs from runtime via GetContainerLogs\n- Supports `--tail` and `--follow` for streaming\n- **Limitation**: Logs lost if container removed before access\n\n### 6.5 Platform-Specific Behaviors\n\n**Linux-Specific**\n- Cgroup v1 (deprecated) vs. v2 (recommended) have different resource enforcement\n- User namespaces supported (UserNamespacesSupport feature gate)\n- Shared PID namespace across pod supported (ShareProcessNamespace)\n- **Deprecation Warning**: cgroup v1 usage logged; migration path to v2 required\n\n**Windows-Specific** (File: `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_windows.go`)\n- No cgroup support; uses Windows Job Objects for resource limits\n- Memory limits via Job Object limits\n- CPU shares via Job scheduling (no precise pinning like Linux)\n- Network isolation via HNS (Host Networking Service)\n- **Limitation**: No fine-grained CPU affinity; device management different\n\n**macOS (Not Supported for Production)**\n- Minimal runtime support; used for local development only\n- No container isolation (containers run as local processes)\n- Not tested in CI; not recommended for real workloads\n\n## 7. File and Directory Map\n\n### Core Runtime Interfaces\n- `pkg/kubelet/container/runtime.go` (450 lines)\n  - `Runtime` interface: SyncPod, KillPod, GarbageCollect, image operations\n  - Container/Pod/Status type definitions\n  - GC policy, port mapping, mount, device types\n\n- `pkg/kubelet/container/container_gc.go` (50 lines)\n  - Wrapper around Runtime.GarbageCollect with policies\n\n### Runtime Implementation\n- `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/` (30+ files)\n  - `kuberuntime_manager.go` (1500+ lines): Main orchestration, SyncPod logic\n  - `kuberuntime_container.go` (500+ lines): Container creation, config generation\n  - `kuberuntime_sandbox.go` (400+ lines): Pod sandbox creation, network setup\n  - `kuberuntime_gc.go` (400+ lines): Garbage collector for containers/sandboxes\n  - `kuberuntime_image.go`: Image pull, list, remove operations\n  - `instrumented_services.go`: Metrics/tracing wrapper around CRI calls\n\n### Resource Management\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go` (320 lines)\n  - `ContainerManager` interface: Start, GetResources, UpdateQOSCgroups, etc.\n\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go` (1000+ lines)\n  - `containerManagerImpl` struct: Cgroup management, system containers\n  - `NewContainerManager`: Factory with cadvisor, subsystem detection\n\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/pod_container_manager_linux.go` (300+ lines)\n  - `PodContainerManager` interface: Exists, EnsureExists, Destroy\n  - Pod-level cgroup setup, QoS hierarchy\n\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/qos_container_manager_linux.go` (300+ lines)\n  - Top-level QoS cgroup management (guaranteed, burstable, besteffort)\n\n### Resource Managers (Pluggable)\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/` (500+ lines)\n  - `Manager` interface: AddContainer, RemoveContainer, Status\n  - Policies: none, static\n  - State: assignment tracking per pod/container\n\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/` (400+ lines)\n  - Similar structure to CPU manager\n  - Memory affinity for NUMA\n\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/` (300+ lines)\n  - Device plugin discovery and allocation\n\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/` (400+ lines)\n  - Topology hints coordination between managers\n  - Hint aggregation and conflict resolution\n\n### Lifecycle Hooks\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/internal_container_lifecycle.go` (60 lines)\n  - `InternalContainerLifecycle` interface: PreCreateContainer, PreStartContainer, PostStopContainer\n  - Implementation coordinating CPU/memory/topology managers\n\n### Supporting Types\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/types.go`: CgroupName, CgroupManager interface, Status types\n- `pkg/kubelet/container/cache.go`: Container hash caching for update detection\n- `pkg/kubelet/container/sync_result.go`: SyncResult aggregation for pod operations\n\n## 8. Summary: Critical Invariants and Design Principles\n\n### Invariants\n1. **One Sandbox Per Pod**: Each pod has exactly one sandbox (network namespace) that all containers share\n2. **Container Order Matters**: Init containers must complete before app containers start; ephemeral containers anytime\n3. **State Convergence**: SyncPod drives pod toward desired state through repeated calls; idempotent\n4. **Cgroup Hierarchy**: Pod cgroups nested under QoS cgroups nested under kubelet cgroup\n5. **GC Safety**: Dead containers only removed if age > minAge AND not from untracked pods (unless forced)\n\n### Design Principles\n1. **Stateless Manager**: Kubelet container manager queries runtime ground truth; no in-memory pod state\n2. **Graceful Termination**: Respect application shutdown; escalate to SIGKILL only after grace period\n3. **Resource Isolation**: QoS guarantees enforced via cgroups; no application-level throttling\n4. **Pluggable Resources**: CPU/memory/device managers plugged via hooks; topology coordinated\n5. **Progressive Pod Lifecycle**: Containers created sequentially per dependencies; not all-or-nothing\n6. **Observability**: Events and metrics on key transitions; ground truth from container runtime\n\nThese principles and invariants ensure Kubernetes pods behave predictably across diverse node configurations and container runtimes while maintaining isolation and resource fairness.\n",

  "content": "# Kubelet Container Manager Architecture Guide\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries\n\nThe kubelet container manager subsystem is responsible for managing the complete lifecycle of containers and pods on a Kubernetes node. It serves as the critical interface between the Kubernetes control plane's desired pod specifications and the actual container runtime (Docker, containerd, CRI-O, etc.) through the Container Runtime Interface (CRI).\n\n### Purpose\n\n- **Container Lifecycle Management**: Create, start, stop, and delete containers with proper ordering and resource allocation\n- **Resource Enforcement**: Apply CPU limits, memory reservations, and device allocations through cgroups\n- **Pod Orchestration**: Coordinate sandbox creation and container dependencies (init containers, ephemeral containers, app containers)\n- **State Reconciliation**: Drive containers toward desired state through repeated synchronization cycles\n- **Garbage Collection**: Remove unused containers and images to prevent resource exhaustion\n\n### Boundaries\n\n**Upstream Dependencies**:\n- **Pod Specifications** (`v1.Pod`): Desired pod configuration from API server\n- **Pod Status**: Current runtime state queried from container runtime\n- **Configuration Sources**: File-based manifests, API server, HTTP endpoints\n- **Resource Allocations**: From device plugins, CPU/memory managers, and topology managers\n\n**Downstream Dependencies**:\n- **Container Runtime Interface (CRI)**: gRPC service for pod/container operations\n- **Cgroup Managers** (Linux): Apply resource limits via cgroup filesystems\n- **Volume Mounts**: Storage subsystem for ephemeral and persistent volumes\n- **Network Plugins**: CNI for pod networking (handled separately in kubelet)\n\n**External Services**:\n- Image registry access for container image pulls\n- Kubelet's own node status and eviction managers\n- Pod lifecycle hooks (pre-start, post-stop handlers)\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 2.1 Runtime Interface Layer\n\n**File**: `pkg/kubelet/container/runtime.go`\n\nThe `Runtime` interface defines the contract that all container runtimes must implement:\n\n```\nRuntime interface provides:\n- SyncPod(ctx, pod, podStatus, pullSecrets, backOff, restartAllContainers) \u2192 PodSyncResult\n  Orchestrates pod creation/updates, the primary entry point\n\n- KillPod(ctx, pod, runningPod, gracePeriodOverride) \u2192 error\n  Terminates all containers in a pod with grace period\n\n- GetPodStatus(ctx, uid, name, namespace) \u2192 *PodStatus\n  Queries runtime for current pod state\n\n- GarbageCollect(ctx, gcPolicy, allSourcesReady, evictNonDeletedPods) \u2192 error\n  Cleans up dead containers per policy\n\n- ImageService: PullImage, ListImages, RemoveImage operations\n```\n\nThis interface allows multiple runtime implementations to be plugged in, though the dominant implementation is `kubeGenericRuntimeManager`.\n\n### 2.2 Concrete Runtime Manager\n\n**File**: `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_manager.go`\n\n`kubeGenericRuntimeManager` is the main orchestration component. It holds:\n\n**Critical Dependencies**:\n- `runtimeService` (internalapi.RuntimeService): gRPC client to actual container runtime\n- `imageService` (internalapi.ImageManagerService): gRPC client for image operations\n- `containerManager` (cm.ContainerManager): Resource allocation and cgroup enforcement\n- `livenessManager`, `readinessManager`, `startupManager`: Probe result caching\n- `containerGC`: Garbage collector for dead containers\n- `internalLifecycle` (cm.InternalContainerLifecycle): Resource manager hooks\n\n**Key Responsibilities**:\n1. Translate Kubernetes pod specs to CRI sandbox/container configurations\n2. Orchestrate container creation sequence (init \u2192 app \u2192 ephemeral)\n3. Manage image pulling with credential providers and retry logic\n4. Coordinate with resource managers for CPU, memory, device allocation\n5. Track container state transitions and generate events\n\n### 2.3 Resource Management Layer\n\n**File**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go`\n\nThe `ContainerManager` interface defines the resource enforcement subsystem:\n\n```\nContainerManager interface manages:\n- System cgroups (kubelet, runtime, system processes)\n- Pod-level cgroups and QoS hierarchies\n- CPU allocation policies (none, static)\n- Memory management and reservation\n- Device plugin resources\n- Topology-aware resource placement\n- Pod admission and pre-flight checks\n- Node allocatable enforcement\n```\n\n**Linux Implementation**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go`\n\nCreates and manages three cgroup hierarchies:\n\n1. **System Cgroups**: Container for kubelet/runtime processes\n2. **Kubelet Cgroups**: Limits on kubelet itself\n3. **Pod Cgroups**: Hierarchy where each pod gets a cgroup based on QoS class\n   - `kubepods` (burstable) \u2192 pod cgroup \u2192 container cgroups\n   - `kubepods-burstable` (burstable) \u2192 pod cgroup \u2192 container cgroups\n   - `kubepods-besteffort` (besteffort) \u2192 pod cgroup \u2192 container cgroups\n\n### 2.4 Pod Container Manager\n\n**File**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/pod_container_manager_linux.go`\n\nManages pod-level cgroup creation and resource configuration:\n\n**Responsibilities**:\n- Create pod-level cgroup if QoS cgroup hierarchy is enabled\n- Apply pod-level CPU and memory limits before container creation\n- Handle MemoryQoS settings (cgroup v2 memory throttling)\n- Enforce PID limits at pod scope\n- Update pod resource configuration dynamically\n\n### 2.5 Resource Managers (Pluggable)\n\nThe container manager coordinates with specialized resource managers through `InternalContainerLifecycle` hooks:\n\n**pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager**: CPU affinity and exclusive CPU allocation\n- Policies: `none` (no affinity), `static` (pinning for Guaranteed pods)\n- Topology-aware placement via NodeInfo topology\n\n**pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager**: Memory affinity for NUMA systems\n- Memory allocation based on topology hints\n- Manages memory reservation per pod\n\n**pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager**: Device plugin resource allocation\n- Tracks device availability from plugins\n- Allocates devices to containers via mounts and environment\n\n**pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager**: Coordinate CPU, memory, and device allocation\n- Collects topology hints from all managers\n- Ensures aligned allocation or fails pod admission\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control and Request Flow\n\n### 3.1 Pod Synchronization Flow (Main Orchestration)\n\n**Entry Point**: `kubeGenericRuntimeManager.SyncPod()` in `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_manager.go:1394`\n\n```\nSyncPod orchestrates 8 sequential steps:\n\nStep 1: Compute Sandbox and Container Changes\n\u251c\u2500 Call computePodActions(pod, podStatus, restartAllContainers)\n\u251c\u2500 Determine what needs killing, creating, or resizing\n\u2514\u2500 Identify sandbox changes (network, security context)\n\nStep 2: Kill Pod Sandbox if Necessary\n\u251c\u2500 If sandbox changed: stop all containers and remove sandbox\n\u2514\u2500 Purge init containers for clean restart\n\nStep 3: Kill Unwanted Containers\n\u251c\u2500 For each container marked for termination\n\u251c\u2500 Call killContainer(pod, containerID, gracePeriod)\n\u2514\u2500 Handle in-place restart container removals\n\nStep 4: Create Pod Sandbox\n\u251c\u2500 generatePodSandboxConfig(pod) \u2192 CRI config\n\u2502  \u251c\u2500 Metadata (name, UID, attempt count)\n\u2502  \u251c\u2500 DNS configuration\n\u2502  \u251c\u2500 Network namespace mode (host/container/none)\n\u2502  \u251c\u2500 Security context (SELinux, AppArmor, seccomp)\n\u2502  \u2514\u2500 RuntimeClass handler lookup\n\u251c\u2500 Call runtimeService.RunPodSandbox(config, handler)\n\u2514\u2500 Store returned sandboxID for containers\n\nStep 5: Create Ephemeral Containers\n\u251c\u2500 For each ephemeral container spec\n\u2514\u2500 createContainer() with copy-on-write semantics\n\nStep 6: Create Init Containers\n\u251c\u2500 Containers execute in order (must complete)\n\u251c\u2500 Each init container waits for previous one\n\u2514\u2500 Handles init container restarts\n\nStep 7: Resize Running Containers (if InPlacePodVerticalScaling)\n\u251c\u2500 For Guaranteed QoS pods\n\u251c\u2500 Call runtimeService.RespawnContainer()\n\u2514\u2500 Adjust CPU/memory allocations\n\nStep 8: Create Normal Application Containers\n\u251c\u2500 Containers run in parallel (optional)\n\u251c\u2500 generateContainerConfig() for each container\n\u251c\u2500 Call createContainer() for each\n\u2514\u2500 Start all containers\n```\n\n### 3.2 Container Creation Sequence\n\n**File**: `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_container.go`\n\nFor each container, the flow is:\n\n```\ncreateContainer(ctx, pod, container):\n  1. generateContainerConfig(pod, container)\n     \u251c\u2500 Image with runtime handler (e.g., nvidia for GPU)\n     \u251c\u2500 Command, args, env variables\n     \u251c\u2500 Mounts (volumes, tmpfs, secrets)\n     \u251c\u2500 Devices (block, character, CDI devices)\n     \u251c\u2500 Port mappings\n     \u2514\u2500 Security context (capabilities, SELinux, user namespace)\n\n  2. Lifecycle hook: PreCreateContainer()\n     \u251c\u2500 Call containerManager.InternalContainerLifecycle\n     \u2514\u2500 (CPU/memory manager setup, topology hints)\n\n  3. Ensure pod container exists (pod cgroup)\n     \u2514\u2500 containerManager.NewPodContainerManager().EnsureExists()\n\n  4. Call runtimeService.CreateContainer(sandboxID, containerConfig)\n     \u2514\u2500 Runtime creates container (not started yet)\n\n  5. Lifecycle hook: PreStartContainer()\n     \u251c\u2500 CPU manager: AddContainer(pod, container, containerID)\n     \u251c\u2500 Memory manager: AddContainer(pod, container, containerID)\n     \u2514\u2500 Topology manager: AddContainer(pod, container, containerID)\n\n  6. Call runtimeService.StartContainer(containerID)\n     \u2514\u2500 Container starts executing\n```\n\n### 3.3 Pod Status Query Flow\n\n**File**: `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_manager.go`\n\nCalled by kubelet's status manager to fetch current pod state:\n\n```\nGetPodStatus(ctx, uid, name, namespace):\n  1. Call runtimeService.PodSandboxStatus(sandboxID)\n  2. For each container in pod:\n     \u2514\u2500 Call runtimeService.ContainerStatus(containerID)\n  3. Extract status fields:\n     \u251c\u2500 State (created, running, exited)\n     \u251c\u2500 Creation/start/finish times\n     \u251c\u2500 Exit code and reason\n     \u251c\u2500 Restart count\n     \u251c\u2500 Resource usage (if available)\n     \u2514\u2500 Mount information\n  4. Aggregate into PodStatus{\n       IPs, ContainerStatuses[], SandboxStatuses[]\n     }\n```\n\n### 3.4 Garbage Collection Flow\n\n**File**: `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_gc.go`\n\nRuns periodically to clean up dead containers:\n\n```\nGarbageCollect(ctx, gcPolicy, allSourcesReady, evictNonDeletedPods):\n  1. List all containers from runtime\n  2. Group containers by (pod UID, container name)\n  3. For each group, keep only N most recent containers per policy:\n     \u251c\u2500 maxPerPodContainer (default 5)\n     \u251c\u2500 maxContainers (default 100)\n     \u2514\u2500 minAge (default 1 minute)\n  4. Mark excess containers for removal\n  5. If allSourcesReady:\n     \u251c\u2500 Also GC containers from unknown pods\n     \u2514\u2500 (pods not in current pod list)\n  6. Stop containers before removal (with grace period)\n  7. Call runtimeService.RemoveContainer(containerID)\n  8. Similarly GC sandboxes (but less aggressive)\n```\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Container Lifecycle Failures\n\n**Sandbox Creation Failures**\n- **Cause**: Network namespace creation fails, SELinux context invalid, resource quota exceeded\n- **Behavior**: Pod marked as failed, containers never created\n- **Recovery**: Retry mechanism with exponential backoff, user must inspect logs and fix spec\n\n**Container Creation Timeouts**\n- **Cause**: Image pull hangs (network), runtime unresponsive\n- **Behavior**: Timeout after default 5 minutes, pod in pending state\n- **Recovery**: Event recorded, retry on next sync cycle\n\n**Resource Allocation Failures**\n- **Cause**: Insufficient CPUs for static affinity, devices unavailable, memory quota exceeded\n- **Behavior**: Pod admission rejected before containers created\n- **Recovery**: Requires resource freeing (other pod eviction) or reducing request\n\n**Container Startup Failures**\n- **Cause**: Application crashed immediately, bad command, permission denied\n- **Behavior**: Container exits quickly, restart policy determines action\n- **Recovery**: Restart loop with exponential backoff (RestartPolicy)\n\n### 4.2 Operational Limits\n\n**Container Count Per Pod**\n- No hard limit in kubelet\n- Practical limit: ~100 containers per pod (scheduling, network overhead)\n- Cgroup management overhead increases linearly\n\n**Container Image Sizes**\n- Runtime-dependent, typically limited by node disk\n- Large images cause longer pull times, delays pod startup\n- Multiple images on same layer share storage (deduplication depends on runtime)\n\n**Grace Period for Shutdown**\n- Default: 30 seconds per pod\n- Minimum: 2 seconds (hardcoded in kuberuntime)\n- Enforced by kubelet + runtime; hard kill (SIGKILL) after grace expires\n\n**Cgroup Resource Limits**\n- CPU shares: integer 2-262144, no unit enforced by cgroup\n- Memory: bytes only, no swap separate from memory (cgroup v1 vs v2 difference)\n- CPU quota: enforces hard limit if cpuCFSQuota enabled\n\n### 4.3 Key Design Tradeoffs\n\n**Sandbox-per-Pod Architecture**\n- **Tradeoff**: One network namespace per pod vs. per-container networking\n- **Rationale**: Simplifies pod networking (all containers share pod IP), matches Kubernetes model\n- **Cost**: Cannot change pod network isolation after creation; sandbox recreation needed\n\n**Preemptive Kill vs. Graceful Termination**\n- **Tradeoff**: Always allow grace period vs. fast cleanup\n- **Rationale**: Respect application shutdown hooks (SIGTERM \u2192 graceful, SIGKILL after)\n- **Cost**: Delayed eviction; can be overridden for node pressure scenarios\n\n**Pod Cgroup Hierarchy**\n- **Tradeoff**: Pod-level cgroup limits vs. per-container granularity\n- **Rationale**: Enforce minimum QoS guarantees at pod scope; QoS class coordination\n- **Cost**: Cannot exceed pod limit even if individual containers idle; less fine-grained control\n\n**Stateless Container Manager**\n- **Tradeoff**: Recompute state every sync cycle vs. in-memory tracking\n- **Rationale**: Resilient to kubelet restarts, always consistent with runtime ground truth\n- **Cost**: Repeated runtime queries; overhead for large pod counts\n\n**ImagePullBackOff vs. Error Distinction**\n- **Tradeoff**: Retry image pulls indefinitely vs. fail fast on bad image\n- **Rationale**: Network transients are common; bad images should retry (user may push fix)\n- **Cost**: User confusion on actually bad images (typos in name, auth failures)\n\n## 5. Extension Points, Customization Hooks, and Associated Risks\n\n### 5.1 Internal Container Lifecycle Hooks\n\n**File**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/internal_container_lifecycle.go`\n\nThree extension points during container creation:\n\n```go\ntype InternalContainerLifecycle interface {\n    // Called after container config generated, before CRI CreateContainer\n    PreCreateContainer(pod, container, containerConfig)\n\n    // Called after runtimeService.StartContainer\n    PreStartContainer(pod, container, containerID)\n\n    // Called after container stopped, before removal\n    PostStopContainer(containerID)\n}\n```\n\n**Current Implementations**:\n- **CPU Manager** (`PreStartContainer`): Pins CPUs for Guaranteed pods\n- **Memory Manager** (`PreStartContainer`): Applies memory affinity\n- **Topology Manager** (`PreStartContainer` and `PostStopContainer`): Coordinates all managers\n\n**Risk**: Bugs in custom hooks block container startup; pod creation hangs if hook panics\n\n### 5.2 RuntimeClass Handler Selection\n\n**File**: `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_sandbox.go:58`\n\nAllows selecting alternative runtime handlers per pod:\n\n```go\nruntimeHandler, err := m.runtimeClassManager.LookupRuntimeHandler(pod.Spec.RuntimeClassName)\n// Passed to runtimeService.RunPodSandbox(..., runtimeHandler)\n```\n\n**Use Cases**:\n- GPU workloads (nvidia, amd handlers)\n- Kata Containers for isolation\n- Custom runtime configurations\n\n**Risk**: Handler misconfiguration silently falls back to default; wrong isolation if handler unavailable\n\n### 5.3 Device Plugin Integration\n\n**File**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/device_manager`\n\nDevice managers expose custom resources:\n\n```go\ncontainerManager.UpdatePluginResources(nodeInfo, podAdmitAttributes)\n// Returns allocated devices via:\ncontainerManager.GetResources(ctx, pod, container)\n```\n\n**Extension Pattern**:\n1. Plugin registers via kubelet plugin watcher\n2. Device manager discovers available resources\n3. On pod admission: topology manager allocates devices\n4. On container creation: GetResources returns mounts, env vars, annotations\n\n**Risk**: Plugin not responding causes pod admission hangs; resource leaks if plugin crashes\n\n### 5.4 Pre-Admit Handlers\n\n**File**: Referenced by `containerManager.GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler()`\n\nPods are admitted before scheduling (kubelet-local gate):\n\n```\nPodAdmitHandler is called:\n  Before any containers created\n  With pod and all current active pods\n  Can reject pod or modify resource allocations\n```\n\n**Use Cases**:\n- Custom admission control (security policies)\n- Dynamic capacity tracking beyond kubelet-reported\n- Pod resource overcommit enforcement\n\n**Risk**: Rejecting pods here bypasses API server validation; inconsistent with scheduler decisions\n\n### 5.5 Image Credential Providers\n\n**File**: `pkg/kubelet/images/pullmanager`\n\nCustom executables can provide registry credentials:\n\n```\nCredential Provider Plugin:\n  Input: image reference\n  Output: username/password or bearer token\n  Executed as subprocess during image pull\n  Can be slow (synchronous in critical path)\n```\n\n**Risk**: Slow credential providers delay all pod startup; credential exposure in logs if not careful\n\n## 6. Operational Implications\n\n### 6.1 Performance Characteristics\n\n**Container Startup Latency**\n- Sandbox creation: 10-50ms (depends on network namespace setup, cgroup creation)\n- Image pull: seconds to minutes (network bound, registry latency)\n- Container creation: 50-200ms per container (runtime-dependent)\n- Container start: 0-5000ms (application dependent, health probe startup)\n- **Total first pod**: seconds to minutes (dominated by image pull)\n- **Total subsequent pod** (cached image): hundreds of milliseconds\n\n**Resource Manager Overhead**\n- CPU manager affinity computation: O(n) where n = CPU count\n- Topology manager hint collection: 3-5ms per container (gathers from CPU/memory/device managers)\n- Cgroup creation: ~1-10ms per pod (filesystem operations)\n- **Scaling limit**: ~100 containers on single node before noticeable delay\n\n**Garbage Collection Overhead**\n- Lists all containers from runtime: O(n) where n = total containers ever created\n- Typical: <100ms for nodes with ~100 total containers\n- **Risk**: GC pause blocks pod operations if many dead containers\n\n### 6.2 Reliability and Resilience\n\n**Recovery from Kubelet Restart**\n- On restart, kubelet queries runtime for all pods and containers\n- Containers continue running under runtime; kubelet re-syncs state\n- **Safe**: Long-running pods unaffected; state consistent from runtime ground truth\n- **Risk**: If container runtime crashed, kubelet cannot detect state; assumes runtime recovery\n\n**Handling Hung Container Runtime**\n- All CRI calls timeout after default 2 minutes\n- Timeout causes pod to be marked failed; events recorded\n- **Limitation**: Cannot forcefully kill runtime; depends on external monitoring\n\n**Orphaned Containers**\n- If kubelet crashes, containers keep running\n- Upon restart: kubelet reattaches via container ID matching\n- **Risk**: If containers deleted from runtime externally, kubelet has stale state (pod never terminates)\n\n### 6.3 Resource Accounting and Limits\n\n**Memory Pressure Handling**\n- Node eviction manager uses cgroup memory.max + usage to trigger eviction\n- Container manager enforces memory.max at pod scope\n- **Limitation**: No memory overcommit enforcement; OOMKiller is last resort\n- **Tuning**: `--memory-manager-policy=static` for guaranteed allocations\n\n**CPU Throttling**\n- CPU limits enforced via cpu.cfs_quota_us / cpu.cfs_period_us\n- CPU manager reserves CPUs for Guaranteed pods (no sharing)\n- **Limitation**: Noisy neighbor problem if bursting pods on same node\n- **Tuning**: `--cpu-manager-policy=static` + CPU topology hints\n\n**Disk I/O Limits**\n- Not enforced by container manager (delegated to runtime/systemd)\n- Cleanup policy for images/logs relies on simple age/count heuristics\n- **Risk**: Slow disk I/O can stall pod startup\n\n### 6.4 Observability and Debugging\n\n**Event Recording**\n- Pod events recorded on key transitions (SandboxChanged, ContainerBackOff, etc.)\n- Events help operators understand failure reasons\n- **Limitation**: No structured logs of internal decisions; must read kubelet logs\n\n**Metrics Exported**\n- `kubelet_pod_worker_duration_seconds`: Time to sync pod\n- `kubelet_container_manager_*`: Resource manager metrics (CPU affinity, etc.)\n- `kubelet_runtime_crio_operations_duration_seconds`: CRI call latencies (per operation type)\n- **Gap**: No metrics on sandbox/container state mismatches\n\n**Pod Log Access**\n- Kubelet reads container logs from runtime via GetContainerLogs\n- Supports `--tail` and `--follow` for streaming\n- **Limitation**: Logs lost if container removed before access\n\n### 6.5 Platform-Specific Behaviors\n\n**Linux-Specific**\n- Cgroup v1 (deprecated) vs. v2 (recommended) have different resource enforcement\n- User namespaces supported (UserNamespacesSupport feature gate)\n- Shared PID namespace across pod supported (ShareProcessNamespace)\n- **Deprecation Warning**: cgroup v1 usage logged; migration path to v2 required\n\n**Windows-Specific** (File: `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_windows.go`)\n- No cgroup support; uses Windows Job Objects for resource limits\n- Memory limits via Job Object limits\n- CPU shares via Job scheduling (no precise pinning like Linux)\n- Network isolation via HNS (Host Networking Service)\n- **Limitation**: No fine-grained CPU affinity; device management different\n\n**macOS (Not Supported for Production)**\n- Minimal runtime support; used for local development only\n- No container isolation (containers run as local processes)\n- Not tested in CI; not recommended for real workloads\n\n## 7. File and Directory Map\n\n### Core Runtime Interfaces\n- `pkg/kubelet/container/runtime.go` (450 lines)\n  - `Runtime` interface: SyncPod, KillPod, GarbageCollect, image operations\n  - Container/Pod/Status type definitions\n  - GC policy, port mapping, mount, device types\n\n- `pkg/kubelet/container/container_gc.go` (50 lines)\n  - Wrapper around Runtime.GarbageCollect with policies\n\n### Runtime Implementation\n- `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/` (30+ files)\n  - `kuberuntime_manager.go` (1500+ lines): Main orchestration, SyncPod logic\n  - `kuberuntime_container.go` (500+ lines): Container creation, config generation\n  - `kuberuntime_sandbox.go` (400+ lines): Pod sandbox creation, network setup\n  - `kuberuntime_gc.go` (400+ lines): Garbage collector for containers/sandboxes\n  - `kuberuntime_image.go`: Image pull, list, remove operations\n  - `instrumented_services.go`: Metrics/tracing wrapper around CRI calls\n\n### Resource Management\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go` (320 lines)\n  - `ContainerManager` interface: Start, GetResources, UpdateQOSCgroups, etc.\n\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go` (1000+ lines)\n  - `containerManagerImpl` struct: Cgroup management, system containers\n  - `NewContainerManager`: Factory with cadvisor, subsystem detection\n\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/pod_container_manager_linux.go` (300+ lines)\n  - `PodContainerManager` interface: Exists, EnsureExists, Destroy\n  - Pod-level cgroup setup, QoS hierarchy\n\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/qos_container_manager_linux.go` (300+ lines)\n  - Top-level QoS cgroup management (guaranteed, burstable, besteffort)\n\n### Resource Managers (Pluggable)\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/` (500+ lines)\n  - `Manager` interface: AddContainer, RemoveContainer, Status\n  - Policies: none, static\n  - State: assignment tracking per pod/container\n\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/` (400+ lines)\n  - Similar structure to CPU manager\n  - Memory affinity for NUMA\n\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/` (300+ lines)\n  - Device plugin discovery and allocation\n\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/` (400+ lines)\n  - Topology hints coordination between managers\n  - Hint aggregation and conflict resolution\n\n### Lifecycle Hooks\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/internal_container_lifecycle.go` (60 lines)\n  - `InternalContainerLifecycle` interface: PreCreateContainer, PreStartContainer, PostStopContainer\n  - Implementation coordinating CPU/memory/topology managers\n\n### Supporting Types\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/types.go`: CgroupName, CgroupManager interface, Status types\n- `pkg/kubelet/container/cache.go`: Container hash caching for update detection\n- `pkg/kubelet/container/sync_result.go`: SyncResult aggregation for pod operations\n\n## 8. Summary: Critical Invariants and Design Principles\n\n### Invariants\n1. **One Sandbox Per Pod**: Each pod has exactly one sandbox (network namespace) that all containers share\n2. **Container Order Matters**: Init containers must complete before app containers start; ephemeral containers anytime\n3. **State Convergence**: SyncPod drives pod toward desired state through repeated calls; idempotent\n4. **Cgroup Hierarchy**: Pod cgroups nested under QoS cgroups nested under kubelet cgroup\n5. **GC Safety**: Dead containers only removed if age > minAge AND not from untracked pods (unless forced)\n\n### Design Principles\n1. **Stateless Manager**: Kubelet container manager queries runtime ground truth; no in-memory pod state\n2. **Graceful Termination**: Respect application shutdown; escalate to SIGKILL only after grace period\n3. **Resource Isolation**: QoS guarantees enforced via cgroups; no application-level throttling\n4. **Pluggable Resources**: CPU/memory/device managers plugged via hooks; topology coordinated\n5. **Progressive Pod Lifecycle**: Containers created sequentially per dependencies; not all-or-nothing\n6. **Observability**: Events and metrics on key transitions; ground truth from container runtime\n\nThese principles and invariants ensure Kubernetes pods behave predictably across diverse node configurations and container runtimes while maintaining isolation and resource fairness.\n",

# Kubelet Container Manager Architecture Guide

## 1. Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries

The kubelet container manager subsystem is responsible for managing the complete lifecycle of containers and pods on a Kubernetes node. It serves as the critical interface between the Kubernetes control plane's desired pod specifications and the actual container runtime (Docker, containerd, CRI-O, etc.) through the Container Runtime Interface (CRI).

### Purpose

- **Container Lifecycle Management**: Create, start, stop, and delete containers with proper ordering and resource allocation
- **Resource Enforcement**: Apply CPU limits, memory reservations, and device allocations through cgroups
- **Pod Orchestration**: Coordinate sandbox creation and container dependencies (init containers, ephemeral containers, app containers)
- **State Reconciliation**: Drive containers toward desired state through repeated synchronization cycles
- **Garbage Collection**: Remove unused containers and images to prevent resource exhaustion

### Boundaries

**Upstream Dependencies**:
- **Pod Specifications** (`v1.Pod`): Desired pod configuration from API server
- **Pod Status**: Current runtime state queried from container runtime
- **Configuration Sources**: File-based manifests, API server, HTTP endpoints
- **Resource Allocations**: From device plugins, CPU/memory managers, and topology managers

**Downstream Dependencies**:
- **Container Runtime Interface (CRI)**: gRPC service for pod/container operations
- **Cgroup Managers** (Linux): Apply resource limits via cgroup filesystems
- **Volume Mounts**: Storage subsystem for ephemeral and persistent volumes
- **Network Plugins**: CNI for pod networking (handled separately in kubelet)

**External Services**:
- Image registry access for container image pull
... (truncated)
